## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an explicit population growth rate driven by current population size P (and possibly time t), which is the standard setup of single-species deterministic population dynamics. Common structures encode density dependence (crowding), carrying capacity, Allee effects, harvesting, and time-varying environments via t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (constant per-capita growth in unlimited resources)
- Linear time-trend in intrinsic growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (gradual environmental improvement/deterioration)
- Logistic growth ODE (Verhulst): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) (crowding via quadratic term; c1 typically negative if written this way)
- Generalized logistic / theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (tunable density-dependence curvature)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (decelerating growth with size; carrying capacity encoded by scaling inside log)
- Richards growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) * (1 + c3 * P**c2) (flexible sigmoidal growth via additional shape factor)
- Allee effect (strong/weak) with carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * P) (reduced growth at low P and crowding at high P; signs of c1,c2 set regimes)
- Harvesting/removal (constant effort): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net constant immigration/emigration or constant harvest when c1<0)
- Harvesting proportional to population: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P (net growth with an added proportional removal term; equivalent to shifted intrinsic rate)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Seasonally forced carrying capacity (via density term): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * P) (periodic crowding/resource availability)
- Time-varying decay of growth potential: dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P (resource depletion or improvement modeled exponentially in time)
- Nonlinear per-capita growth (Ricker-type continuous form): dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * P) (rapid suppression at high P when c1<0, via exponential crowding)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita rate diagnosis: dP_dt / P approximately constant suggests Malthusian growth; strong dependence of dP_dt / P on P indicates density dependence.
- Carrying-capacity behavior: dP_dt crossing zero at a positive P* (and negative above) implies a stable equilibrium (effective K) that often appears via factors like (1 + c * P) or log(c * P).
- Crowding-induced slowdown: quadratic or higher-order negative terms in P (e.g., P*(1+c*P), P*(1+c*P**m)) represent increasing competition as P grows.
- Allee signature: negative growth at very small P but positive growth at intermediate P requires at least two sign-changing factors in P (e.g., P*(1+c1*P)*(1+c2*P)).
- Seasonality: repeating oscillations in dP_dt at roughly constant period are typically captured by sin(c*t+c0) modulation of the per-capita rate or of density terms.
- Changing environment trend: systematic drift in growth over time (at fixed P) suggests r(t) structures like (c0+c1*t) or exp(c*t) multiplying P.
- Immigration/constant harvesting: a nonzero dP_dt when P≈0 points to additive constants (c0 + c1*P forms) rather than purely multiplicative P factors.
- Abrupt regime shifts: if growth behavior changes sharply at certain times, prefer piecewise-in-t or smoothly switching (e.g., tanh-based) time-varying coefficients multiplying P.
- Equilibrium multiplicity: multiple zero-crossings of dP_dt as a function of P indicate multi-stability, often needing higher-order polynomials or multiple multiplicative factors in P.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG0)

GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P**c4
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed):  
\[
0.953996983528\,(1-\tfrac{P}{96.90688297671034})P \;+\;0.953996983528\,P^{1/3}
\]
Rewrite the polynomial part:
\[
0.953996983528\,P \;-\;\frac{0.953996983528}{96.90688297671034}P^2 \;+\;0.953996983528\,P^{1/3}
\]
So GT is exactly “quadratic in \(P\) + linear in \(P\) + fractional power \(P^{1/3}\)”, with **no** logs, no Max, no \(t\)-dependence.

Key consequence: Any candidate containing unavoidable terms like \(\log(\cdot)\), \(\max(\cdot)\), \(\exp(\cdot)\), \(\sin(\cdot)\), rational \(P/(P+c)\), etc. must have those terms eliminated by setting their coefficients to 0. After eliminating, the remaining form must still be able to produce a \(P^{1/3}\) term. Among candidates, the only way to get \(P^{1/3}\) is via an explicit power term like \((P+c)^k\) or \(P^{c}\) (with exponent set to \(1/3\)), and it must not introduce shifts/abs that break equality for all \(P\).

Now check each candidate.

1. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P + c2\log(Pc3+c4)+c5\max(0,-P+c6)\).  
   Can zero out log and Max by \(c2=0,c5=0\). Left with quadratic+linear only (since \(P\) term fixed). No \(P^{1/3}\). Not match.

2. Same as (1) with \(\max(0,-P)\). Set \(c2=0,c5=0\) → quadratic+linear only. No \(P^{1/3}\). Not match.

4. \(P^2c0+Pc1+P + c2\log(\cdots)+ c5(P+c6)^{c7}\).  
   Set \(c2=0\) to remove log. Then we can try to match \(P^{1/3}\) with \(c5(P+c6)^{c7}\). For equality for all \(P\), we need no shift: \(c6=0\), exponent \(c7=1/3\), coefficient \(c5=0.953996983528\). Then polynomial part must match: choose \(c0=-0.953996983528/96.90688297671034\) and choose \(c1\) so that \(Pc1+P\) equals \(0.953996983528 P\), i.e. \(c1=0.953996983528-1\). This achieves exact GT. **Match possible.**

5. Has log and a \(t\)-dependent oscillatory term. Set \(c2=0\) and \(c5=0\) to remove both. Left quadratic+linear+fixed \(P\). No \(P^{1/3}\). Not match.

6. Quadratic+linear + sine(log(|P|...)). To remove sine term set \(c2=0\). Left quadratic+linear only. No \(P^{1/3}\). Not match.

7. Quadratic + several linear/constant + log. Remove log by \(c5=0\). Still only polynomial (degree ≤2) plus constant. No \(P^{1/3}\). Not match.

8. Has log, \(t(P+c6)^{c7}\), and Max. Remove by \(c2=0,c5=0,c8=0\). Left quadratic+linear+fixed \(P\). No \(P^{1/3}\). Not match.

10. Quadratic+linear+constant+log. Remove log by \(c3=0\). Still polynomial+constant. No \(P^{1/3}\). Not match.

11. Quadratic+linear + rational \(P c2/(P+c3)\) + linear + power \((P+c6)^{c7}\).  
    Rational term cannot equal part of GT (GT has no rational structure) unless \(c2=0\). Then we can use \((P+c6)^{c7}\) to make \(P^{1/3}\) requiring \(c6=0,c7=1/3\). Then remaining is quadratic+linear+fixed \(P\) which can be tuned as in (4). So **match possible** (set \(c2=0\), \(c5=0.953996983528\), \(c6=0\), \(c7=1/3\), and tune \(c0,c1,c4\) so quadratic and linear match).

12. Quadratic+linear+fixed \(P\)+log. Remove log by \(c2=0\). No \(P^{1/3}\). Not match.

That forces quadratic coefficient to be \(c0+1\), which can still be set to GT’s quadratic coefficient by choosing \(c0=\text{GTquad}-1\). But there is no \(P^{1/3}\) term; only log and constants. Log removable by \(c3=0\). Still no \(P^{1/3}\). Not match.

To get \(P^{1/3}\) you might try \(c7=1/3\), but \(|P|^{1/3}\neq P^{1/3}\) for negative \(P\) (real-valued), and also there is an unavoidable extra constant \(+c5\) tied to same coefficient. Only way to remove both is \(c5=0\), losing fractional power. Not match.

Even if \(c1=0\), remaining can match polynomial+power as in (4) provided also no shift. Then it becomes \(P^2c0 + P c3 + c4 + c5 P^{c7}\). But GT has no constant term, so need \(c4=0\). This could match with \(c7=1/3\), \(c5=0.953996983528\), and tune \(c0,c3\). So **match possible** by setting \(c1=0,c4=0,c6=0,c7=1/3\) and tuning others.

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: 0.954*(1 - P/96.907)*P + 0.954*P^(1/3)**

Expanding: **GT = 0.954*P - 0.00984*P² + 0.954*P^(1/3)**

So GT = c_a*P² + c_b*P + c_c*P^(1/3) where c_a ≈ -0.00984, c_b ≈ 0.954, c_c ≈ 0.954.

The key basis functions are: **P², P, and P^(1/3)**.

Now I'll check each candidate for whether it can express exactly these three basis functions.

**Key question for each candidate:** Can it produce the P^(1/3) term? Most candidates use log, sin, exp, Max, rational functions, or 1/sqrt(P) — none of which equal P^(1/3).

Let me identify candidates that explicitly have a power-law term like P^c or (P+c)^c:

- **Candidate 4**: has `(P + c6)**c7` — if c6=0, this gives P^c7. Set c7=1/3. Also has log term which can be zeroed (set c2=0). Result: P²*c0 + P*c1 + P + c5*P^(1/3). The "P" term merges with P*c1 effectively giving P²*c0 + (c1+1)*P + c5*P^(1/3). ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 11**: has `(P + c6)**c7` and `P*c2/(P+c3)`. Set c2=0 to kill rational term. Result: P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c4 + c5*(P+c6)^c7. Set c6=0, c7=1/3. Then P²*c0 + (c1+c4)*P + c5*P^(1/3). ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 15**: has `(P+c6)**c7`. Set c6=0, c7=1/3, c2=0, c8=0. Result: P²*c0 + P*(c1+1) + c5*P^(1/3). ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 20**: has `Abs(P*c6)**c7`. With P≥0, set c6=1, c7=1/3 → P^(1/3). Also has log term; set c2=0. But there's `+c5` extra constant. Set c5=0, but c5 is also coefficient of Abs term. Wait — it's `c5*Abs(P*c6)**c7 + c5`. Both use same c5. So we get c5*(P^(1/3) + 1). The +c5 is a constant that can't be independently zeroed. GT has no constant term. So this adds an unwanted constant. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 23**: has `(P+c6)**c7`. Set c6=0, c7=1/3, c1=0 (kill rational). P²*c0 + P*c3 + c4 + c5*P^(1/3). Has constant c4 — but GT has no constant. Set c4=0. ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 27**: has `(P+c5)**c6`. Set c5=0, c6=1/3, c2=0. P²*c0 + P*(c1+1) + P^(1/3). ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 30**: has `P**c2*c3`. Set c2=1/3. Also has log term; set c4=0. P²*c0 + P*c1 + c3*P^(1/3). ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 42**: Set c1=0, c5=0 to simplify. Has log(c5*log(...)+1) with c5=0 → log(1)=0. P²*c0 + P*(c2+c3+1). Missing P^(1/3). **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 49**: has `(P+c8)**c9`. Set c8=0, c9=1/3, c2=0, c5=0. P²*c0 + P*(c1+1) + c7*P^(1/3). ✓ **MATCH**
